                  </quote> (S, M) or, as Fr relates it, <foreign lang="ar">كُلَّ قَصُورَةً</foreign> (S) [<hi rend="ital">And thou art the person who hath made every female confined within the house to be an object of love to me, while the females confined within the house know not that: I mean those confined within the curtained canopies: I do not mean the short in step: the worst of women are the short and compressed</hi>]. And a poet says <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَأَهْوَى مِنَ النِّسوَانِ كُلَّ قَصِيرَةٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَهَا نَسَبٌ فِى الصَّالِحِينَ قَصِيرُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And I love, of women, every one that is confined within the house, that has a short pedigree, among the good</hi>]; i. e., every   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35781-8" target="مَقْصُورَة" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, of whom it suffices to mention her descent from her father, because of his being well known. (M.) Hence, in the Kur, [lv. 72,] <foreign lang="ar">حُورٌ مَقْصُورَاتٌ فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الخِيَامِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Damsels having eyes whereof the white is intensely white and the black intensely black,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">confined in the pavilions,</hi> (Az, Msb,) which are of pearls, for their husbands; (Az;) <hi rend="ital">concealed by curtains:</hi> (Az, Bd:) or <hi rend="ital">confined to their husbands, and not raising their eyes to others:</hi> (Fr:) or <hi rend="ital">having their eyes restricted to their husbands.</hi> (Bd.) And
